There are\\n69:     no implicit dependencies between numbered migrations - the numbering is\\n70:     merely a convention to aid file listing. Every new numbered migration\\n71:     has a declared dependency to the previous number, meaning that VCS\\n72:     branch merges can be detected and resolved.\\n73: \\n74:     Migrations files can be marked as replacing another set of migrations -\\n75:     this is to support the \\\"squash\\\" feature. The graph handler isn't\\n76:     responsible for these; instead, the code to load them in here should\\n77:     examine the migration files and if the replaced migrations are all either\\n78:     unapplied or not present, it should ignore the replaced ones, load in just\\n79:     the replacing migration, and repoint any dependencies that pointed to the\\n80:     replaced migrations to point to the replacing one.\\n81: \\n82:     A node should be a tuple: (app_path, migration_name). Any\\n128:         dependencies that were referencing them are changed to reference the\\n129:         `replacement` node instead.\\n130:         \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n131:         # Cast list of replaced keys to set to speed up lookup later.\\n132:         replaced = set(replaced)\\n133:         try:\\n134:             replacement_node = self.node_map[replacement]\\n135:         except KeyError as err:\\n136:             raise NodeNotFoundError(\\n137:                 \\\"Unable to find replacement node %r. Almost. Remove the\\n164:         replacement node `replacement` and remap its child nodes to `replaced`\\n165:         - the list of nodes it would have replaced. Don't remap its parent\\n166:         nodes as they are expected to be correct already.\\n167:         \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n168:         self.nodes.pop(replacement, None)\\n169:         try:\\n170:             replacement_node = self.node_map.pop(replacement)\\n171:         except KeyError as err:\\n172:             raise NodeNotFoundError(\\n173:                 \\\"Unable to remove replacement node %r. start, forwards=True):\\n223:         \\\"\\\"\\\"Iterative depth-first search for finding dependencies.\\\"\\\"\\\"\\n224:         visited = []\\n225:         visited_set = set()\\n226:         stack = [(start, False)]\\n227:         while stack:\\n228:             node, processed = stack.pop()\\n229:             if node in visited_set:\\n230:                 pass\\n231:             elif processed:\\n232:                 visited_set.add(node)\\n233:                 visited.append(node.key)\\n234:             else:\\n235:                 stack.append((node, True))\\n236: \\n242:     def root_nodes(self, app=None):\\n243:         \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n244:         Return all root nodes - that is, nodes with no dependencies inside\\n245:         their app. These are the starting point for an app.\\n246:         \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n247:         roots = set()\\n248:         for node in self.nodes:\\n249:             if all(key[0] != node[0] for key in self.node_map[node].parents) and (\\n250:                 not app or app == node[0]\\n251:             ):\\n252:                 roots.add(node)\\n253:         return sorted(roots)\\n254: \\n255:     def leaf_nodes(self, app=None):\\n256:         \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n257:         Return all leaf nodes - that is, nodes with no dependents in their app.\\n258:         These are the \\\"most current\\\" version of an app's schema.\\n259:         Having more than one per app is technically an error, but one that\\n260:         gets handled further up, in the interactive command - it's usually the\\n261:         result of a VCS merge and needs some user input.\\n262:         \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n263:         leaves = set()\\n264:         for node in self.nodes:\\n265:             if all(key[0] != sorted(leaves)\\n270: \\n271:     def ensure_not_cyclic(self):\\n272:         # Algo from GvR:\\n273:         # https://neopythonic.blogspot.com/2009/01/detecting-cycles-in-directed-graph.html\\n274:         todo = set(self.nodes)\\n275:         while todo:\\n276:             node = todo.pop()\\n277:             stack = [node]\\n278:             while stack:\\n279:                 top = stack[-1]\\n280:                 for child in self.node_map[top].children:\\n281:                     # Use child.key instead of child to speed up the frequent\\n282:                     # hashing.\\n283:                     node = child.key\\n284:                     if node in stack:\\n285:                         cycle = stack[stack.index(node) :]\\n286:                         raise CircularDependencyError(\\n287:                             \\\", \\\".join(\\\"%s.%s\\\" % n for n in cycle)\\n288:                         )\\n289:                     if node in todo:\\n290:                         stack.append(node)\\n291:                         todo.remove(node)\\n292:                         break\\n293:                 else:\\n294:                     node = stack.pop()\\n295: \\n296:     def __str__(self):\\n297:         return \\\"Graph: %s nodes, %s edges\\\" % self._nodes_and_edges()\\n298: \\n299:     def __repr__(self):\\n300:         nodes, edges = self._nodes_and_edges()\\n301:         return \\\"<%s: nodes=%s, edges=%s>\\\" % (self.__class__.__name__, nodes, edges)\\n302: \\n303:     def _nodes_and_edges(self):\\n304:         return \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n318:         Given a migration node or nodes, return a complete ProjectState for it.\\n319:         If at_end is False, return the state before the migration has run.\\n320:         If compliance is implemented across multiple Python source files in the django/django repository. The architecture consists of four main components:\\n\\n1. **Squash Migration Generator** (django/core/management/commands/squashmigrations.py): The Command class's handle() method generates new squashed migrations by collecting operations and dependencies from a range of migrations, optimizing them using MigrationOptimizer, and creating a new Migration instance with the `replaces` attribute set to the list of replaced migrations.\\n\\n2. **Replaced-Migrations Tracking** (django/db/migrations/loader.py): The MigrationLoader class maintains a replacements dictionary during build_graph() that tracks all migrations marked with non-empty `replaces` attributes. The replace_migration() method processes these tracked migrations and validates for circular dependencies, raising CommandError if a cyclical squash replacement is detected. The _resolve_replaced_migration_keys() method recursively resolves the actual replaced migrations even when multiple squashed migrations reference each other.\\n\\n3. **Dependency Graph Validation After Squashing** (django/db/migrations/graph.py): The MigrationGraph class provides two critical methods for handling squashed migrations:\\n   - remove_replaced_nodes(): Removes replaced migration nodes from the graph and remaps dependencies pointing to them to the replacement node\\n   - remove_replacement_node(): The inverse operation that removes a replacement node and remaps its dependents to the replaced nodes (used when a squashed migration is partially applied)\\n   - validate_consistency(): Ensures no dummy nodes remain in the graph, which would indicate missing dependencies\\n\\n4. **Squash Completeness Check** (django/db/migrations/executor.py): The check_replacements() method in MigrationExecutor marks replacement migrations as applied when all their replaced migrations are applied, using the loader's all_replaced_applied() method which recursively checks if all replaced migrations (including those transitively replaced by other squashed migrations) have been applied in the database.\\n\\nAdditional supporting files include:\\n- django/db/migrations/migration.py: Defines the Migration base class with the `replaces` attribute\\n- django/db/migrations/optimizer.py: Optimizes operations sequences during squash generation\\n- django/db/migrations/exceptions.py: Defines exception types (NodeNotFoundError, InconsistentMigrationHistory, CircularDependencyError) used for validation\\n- django/db/migrations/writer.py: Serializes and writes migration files\\n- django/db/migrations/recorder.py: Records applied migration status in the database\\n\\nThe entire flow ensures that squashed migrations can coexist with their replaced migrations, Django intelligently switches between them based on migration history state, and circular dependency scenarios are detected and prevented.\"\n}\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":10,"cache_creation_input_tokens":1753,"cache_read_input_tokens":79914,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":1753},"output_tokens":3,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"be08b2d8-b844-4bd6-a705-8651fb0c0b3d","uuid":"c41f7cd9-0d21-4dca-87d1-cd8f6f07424f"}

compliance is implemented across multiple Python source files in the django/django repository. The architecture consists of four main components:\\n\\n1. **Squash Migration Generator** (django/core/management/commands/squashmigrations.py): The Command class's handle() method generates new squashed migrations by collecting operations and dependencies from a range of migrations, optimizing them using MigrationOptimizer, and creating a new Migration instance with the `replaces` attribute set to the list of replaced migrations.\\n\\n2. **Replaced-Migrations Tracking** (django/db/migrations/loader.py): The MigrationLoader class maintains a replacements dictionary during build_graph() that tracks all migrations marked with non-empty `replaces` attributes. The replace_migration() method processes these tracked migrations and validates for circular dependencies, raising CommandError if a cyclical squash replacement is detected. The _resolve_replaced_migration_keys() method recursively resolves the actual replaced migrations even when multiple squashed migrations reference each other.\\n\\n3. **Dependency Graph Validation After Squashing** (django/db/migrations/graph.py): The MigrationGraph class provides two critical methods for handling squashed migrations:\\n   - remove_replaced_nodes(): Removes replaced migration nodes from the graph and remaps dependencies pointing to them to the replacement node\\n   - remove_replacement_node(): The inverse operation that removes a replacement node and remaps its dependents to the replaced nodes (used when a squashed migration is partially applied)\\n   - validate_consistency(): Ensures no dummy nodes remain in the graph, which would indicate missing dependencies\\n\\n4. **Squash Completeness Check** (django/db/migrations/executor.py): The check_replacements() method in MigrationExecutor marks replacement migrations as applied when all their replaced migrations are applied, using the loader's all_replaced_applied() method which recursively checks if all replaced migrations (including those transitively replaced by other squashed migrations) have been applied in the database.\\n\\nAdditional supporting files include:\\n- django/db/migrations/migration.py: Defines the Migration base class with the `replaces` attribute\\n- django/db/migrations/optimizer.py: Optimizes operations sequences during squash generation\\n- django/db/migrations/exceptions.py: Defines exception types (NodeNotFoundError, InconsistentMigrationHistory, CircularDependencyError) used for validation\\n- django/db/migrations/writer.py: Serializes and writes migration files\\n- django/db/migrations/recorder.py: Records applied migration status in the database\\n\\nThe entire flow ensures that squashed migrations can coexist with their replaced migrations, Django intelligently switches between them based on migration history state, and circular dependency scenarios are detected and prevented.\"\n}\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}
